Module ansa.report

ansa.report.
HeightOfSlide
(
unit
:
float
)
→
float
#
Deprecated since version 20.1.0:
Use
ansa.report.Report.get_slide_size()
instead.
This function returns the height of the report slide.
Parameters
:
unit
float
Refers to the unit of measurement of the height. Its possible values are:
- ‘mm’ : Millimeters
- ‘pixel’ : Pixels.
Returns
:
float
This function returns as float the height of the report slide in the given unit of measurement.
Examples
# PYTHON script
import
ansa
from
ansa
import
report
def
main
():
h_mm
=
report
.
HeightOfSlide
(
"mm"
)
# The height of the report slide in millimeter
h_px
=
report
.
HeightOfSlide
(
"pixel"
)
# The height of the report slide in pixels
print
(
"The height of the slide is "
+
str
(
h_mm
)
+
" mm or "
+
str
(
h_px
)
+
"px."
)

ansa.report.
NamesOfAllSlides
(
)
→
Iterable
[
str
]
#
This function get names of all existing slides of the report.
Returns
:
Iterable[str]
It returns a list where each member of the list is a string referring to the name of an existing slide of the report.
Upon failure, an empty list is returned.
Examples
# PYTHON script
import
ansa
from
ansa
import
report
def
main
():
all_slides
=
report
.
NamesOfAllSlides
()
for
slide_name
in
all_slides
:
print
(
slide_name
)

ansa.report.
TextOfReportTextbox
(
slide_name
:
str
,
textbox_name
:
str
,
text_type
:
int
)
→
str
#
Deprecated since version 20.1.0:
Use
ansa.report.Textbox.get_text()
instead.
This function gets the text of a textbox of a given toolbar.
Parameters
:
slide_name
str
Name of the slide
textbox_name
str
Name of the textbox
text_type
int
If value of argument “text_type” is 0 then the text after the quantification of any variables is returned, else the original text is returned.
Returns
:
str
Upon success, it returns a string referring to the text of the textbox of the given slide.
Upon failure, it returns an empty string.
Notes
This functions works for the active report composer.
Examples
# PYTHON script
import
ansa
from
ansa
import
report
def
main
():
slide_name
=
"Slide 1"
textbox_name
=
"Textbox 1"
text_type
=
1
text
=
report
.
TextOfReportTextbox
(
slide_name
,
textbox_name
,
text_type
)
print
(
text
)
if

==
"__main__"

→

[
float
]
#
This function returns the width of the specified columns for a given Excel table in the specified unit.
Parameters
:
slide_name
str
Name of the slide.
table_name
str
Name of the table.
sheet_name
str
Name of the sheet.
columns
Iterable[int]
A list with the numbers of the columns of interest (Numbering starts from 0).
unit
str
The unit of interest:
-pt
-mm
-pixel
Returns
:
Iterable[float]
The function returns a list that contains columns’ width.
Notes
The function works for the active Report Composer.
Examples
# PYTHON script
import
ansa
from
ansa
import
report

main
():

=
"Slide 1"

=
"Table 1"
sheet_name
=
"Sheet1"
columns
=
[
0
,
1
,
3
]
unit
=
"pt"

=

.
WidthOfSpreadsheetColumns
(

,

,
sheet_name
,
columns
,
unit
)

(

NamesOfAllShapes
(
slide_name
:
str
)
→
dict
#
This function returns a map containing the names of the shapes in the given slide, grouped by shape type.
Parameters
:
slide_name
str
Name of the slide
Returns
:
dict
It returns a dictionary which contains, the shape types as keys, and lists of shape names as values.
Upon failure, an empty dictionary is returned.
See also
ansa.report.NamesOfAllSlides
Notes
This functions works for the active report composer.
Examples
# PYTHON script
import
ansa
from
ansa
import
report
def
main
():
slide_name
=
"Slide 1"
all_shapes
=
report
.
NamesOfAllShapes
(
slide_name
)
for
shape_type
in
all_shapes
:
print
(
shape_type
[
0
])
for
shape
in
shape_type
[
1
]:
print
(
shape
)

ansa.report.
CreateReport
(
name
:
str
)
→
Report
#
Creates a report composer window with the provided name, or a unique generated name if one is not provided. Returns None if a name is provided and a report with that name already exists.
Parameters
:
name
str, optional
Name of the new report composer window.
Returns
:
Report
Upon success returns an object of type meta.report.Report
Upon failure returns None.
See also
ansa.report.Report
,
ansa.report.Reports
Notes
Creation fails when a report composer window with the same name exists.
Examples
# PYTHON script
import
ansa
from
ansa
import
report
def
main
():
# Create new report
r
=
report
.
CreateReport
()
print
(
r
)
# Or
name
=
"Report 1"
r
=
report
.
CreateReport
(
name
)
print
(
r
)

==
"__main__"
:

DeleteReport
(
report
:
ansa.report.Report
|
str
)
→
bool
#
Deletes the given report from META. This action invalidates the object.
Parameters
:
report
Report | str
Either a report name as a string or a meta.report.Report object.
Returns
:
bool
Upon success returns True
Upon failure returns False.
See also
ansa.report.Report
,
ansa.report.CreateReport
,
ansa.report.Reports
Examples
# PYTHON script

ansa
from
ansa
import
report
def
main
():
# Create new report
r
=
report
.
CreateReport
()
# Delete report
ret
=
report
.
DeleteReport
(
r
)

(

)

ansa.report.
CreateReportFilter
(
type
:
str
,
name
:
str
,
operator
:
str
,
value
:
str
,
value2
:
str
)
→
ReportFilter
#
Creates a report filter.
Parameters
:
type
str
Available values are listed below. Note that the ‘tag’ type also requires the rest of the arguments to be specified, a name, operator, and at least one value (depending on the operator).
‘presentation’
‘slide’
‘element’
‘tag’
name
str, optional
The tag name to search for.
operator
str, optional
Available values are listed below, note that some operators require a value2 argument as well.
‘equal’
‘less’
‘greater’
‘less_equal’
‘greater_equal’
‘not_equal’
‘between’
‘not_between’
‘contains’
‘not_contains’
‘starts_with’
‘not_starts_with’
‘ends_with’
‘not_ends_with’
‘reg_expression’
‘not_reg_expression’
value
str, optional
The tag value that is matched against the value of the tags in the report files using the specified operator.
value2
str, optional
A second optional value required by operators  ‘between’ and ‘not_between’.
Returns
:
ReportFilter
meta.report.ReportFilter
See also
ansa.report.ReportFilter
Examples
# PYTHON script
import
ansa
from
ansa
import
report
def
main
():
directory
=
"../"
type
=
"presentation"
presFilter
=
report
.
CreateReportFilter
(
"presentation"
)
# OR
type
=
"tag"
name
=
"tag1"
operator
=
"equal"
value
=
"value1"
tagFilter
=
report
.
CreateReportFilter
(
type
,
name
,
operator
,
value
)
presFilter
.
add_child
(
tagFilter
)
print
(
presFilter
)
print
(
presFilter
.
get_children
())
print
(
presFilter
.
search
(
directory
))

class
ansa.report.
Report
(
report_name
:
str
)
#
A report composer window in META. It can be used to create and edit reports.
Reports can be loaded from and exported to pptx files.
Parameters
:
report_name
str
Report Composer window name.
Returns
:
None
name
:
str
=
None
#
Report composer window name.
open
(
filename
:
str
,
load_shape_names
:
bool
=
True
,
load_slide_names
:
bool
=
True
)
→
bool
#
Loads a report from the specified pptx file.
Parameters
:
filename
str
Path to pptx file.
load_shape_names
bool, optional
Whether to load the shape names from the pptx file or not. Default value is True.
load_slide_names
bool, optional
Whether to load the slide, layout, and master names from the pptx file or not. Default value is True.
Returns
:
bool
save
(
filename
:
str
,
options
:
dict
)
→
bool
#
Export the report to a pptx file.
Parameters
:
filename
str
Path to pptx file.
options
dict, optional
Dictionary with string keys. Each key corresponds to an option. The available keys are listed below along with the type of value that is expected.
‘redraw_excel_tables’ : boolean
‘excel_snapshots’ : boolean
‘vbscript_redraw’ : boolean
‘shrink_autofit’ : boolean
‘excel_2003_compatibility’ : boolean
‘excel_xls_compatibility’ : boolean
‘output_unparsed_text’ : boolean
‘compress_images_ppi’ : integer (supported values: 220, 150, 96)
Returns
:
bool
reset
(
)
→
bool
#
Clears the report composer leaving only one empty slide.
Returns
:
bool
get_slide
(
slide
:
str
|
int
)
→
Slide
#
Returns the slide specified either by its name or its id.
Parameters
:
slide
str | int
Either the name of the slide as a string or the position of the slide as an integer. Slide numbering starts from 1.
Returns
:
Slide
meta.report.Slide

index

set_slide_size
(
size
:
Iterable
[
float
]
,
unit
:
str
,
type
:
str
,
orientation
:
str
)
→
bool
#
Sets the slide width and height either using the ‘size’ argument or by selecting one of the predefined sizes with the combination of ‘type’ and ‘orientation’ arguments. If ‘size’ is used an optional unit can be provided.
Parameters
:
size
Iterable[float], optional
Either a list or 2-tuple that contains the width and height.
unit
str, optional
Unit of the given width and height.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘mm’.
‘emu’
‘cm’
‘mm’
‘inch’
‘pt’
‘pc’
‘pixel’
type
str, optional
When using this option an orientation must also be provided. Available values are:
‘a0’  :  841 x 1189 mm
‘a1’  :  594 x 841 mm
‘a2’  :  420 x 594 mm
‘a3’  :  297 x 420 mm
‘a4’  :  210 x 297 mm, 8.26 x 11.69 inches
‘a5’  :  148 x 210 mm
‘a6’  :  105 x 148 mm
‘a7’  :  74 x 105 mm
‘a8’  :  52 x 74 mm
‘a9’  :  37 x 52 mm
‘b0’  :  1000 x 1414 mm
‘b1’  :  707 x 1000 mm
‘b2’  :  500 x 707 mm
‘b3’  :  353 x 500 mm
‘b4’  :  250 x 353 mm
‘b5’  :  176 x 250 mm, 6.93 x 9.84 inches
‘b6’  :  125 x 176 mm
‘b7’  :  88 x 125 mm
‘b8’  :  62 x 88 mm
‘b9’  :  33 x 62 mm
‘b10’  :  31 x 44 mm
‘c5e’  :  163 x 229 mm
‘comm10e’  :  105 x 241 mm, u.s. common 10 envelope
‘dle’  :  110 x 220 mm
‘executive’  :  190.5 x 254 mm, 7.5 x 10 inches,
‘folio’  :  210 x 330 mm
‘ledger’  :  431.8 x 279.4 mm
‘legal’  :  215.9 x 355.6 mm, 8.5 x 14 inches,
‘letter’  :  215.9 x 279.4 mm, 8.5 x 11 inches,
‘tabloid’  :  279.4 x 431.8 mm
‘film35mm’  :  36 x 24 mm
‘screen16_9’  :  254 x 143.002 mm, 10 x 5.63 in
‘screen16_10’  :  254 x 158.75 mm, 10 x 6.25 in
‘screen4_3’  :         254 x 190.5 mm, 10 x 7.5 in
orientation
str, optional
Either ‘portrait’ or ‘landscape’.
Returns
:
bool
get_slide_size
(
unit
:
str
)
→
list
[
float
]
#
Returns the width and height of a slide.
Parameters
:
unit
str, optional
Unit of the returned width and height.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘mm’.
‘emu’
‘cm’
‘mm’
‘inch’
‘pt’
‘pc’
‘pixel’
Returns
:
list[float]
A list that contains the width and height in the requested units.

Freeform
#
Creates a new freeform shape in the slide. The new shape is returned.
Parameters
:
points
list
A non-empty list of pairs of x, y coordinates.
unit
str, optional
Unit of the given width and height.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions
name
str, optional
Shape name.
Returns
:
Freeform
meta.report.Freeform

‘sys_dot_line’

get_text_style
(
position
:
int
)
→
dict
#
Returns the text style in the form of a python dictionary. The dictionary contains the same keys and can be applied directly to the set_text_style function. An optional position argument can be used to return the style of a specific character in the text.
Parameters
:
position
int, optional
Index of the character in the text whose style is returned. Indexing starts at 1. If undefined the style of the last character is returned.
Returns
:
dict
Python dictionary with the following text style options.font_family     stringfont_size       integerbold            booleanitalic          booleanunderline       booleanstrike_through  booleansuperscript     booleansubscript       booleantext_color      meta.windows.Colortext_align      string                        ‘left’                        ‘center’                        ‘right’                        ‘justify’shape_align     string                        ‘top’                        ‘middle’                        ‘bottom’                        ‘top_center’                        ‘middle_center’                        ‘bottom_center’autofit         string                        ‘no_autofit’                        ‘shrink_text_on_overflow’                        ‘resize_shape_to_fit_text’wrap            boolean

#
Return the coordinates of the top left corner of the shape.
Parameters
:
unit
str, optional
Unit of the returned coordinates.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions
Returns
:
Iterable[float]
List that contains the x an y coordinates.

float
]
,

:

)

Parameters

- ‘pt’

- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions

:
str
)
→
bool
#
Set various line style options. All arguments are optional, any number of them can be used. The result is visible only when fill is ‘solid_line’.
Parameters
:
fill
str, optional
The available values are:
- ‘no_line’
- ‘solid_line’
color
windows.Color, optional
meta.windows.Color
width
float, optional
Line width.
dash
str, optional
One of the following predefined dash patterns:
‘solid_line’
‘dash_line’
‘dot_line’
‘dash_dot_line’
‘lg_dash_line’
‘lg_dash_dot_line’
‘lg_dash_dot_dot_line’
‘sys_dash_line’
‘sys_dash_dot_line’
‘sys_dash_dot_dot_line’
‘sys_dot_line’
‘custom_dash_line’
custom_dash_pattern
str, optional
A series of 1’s and 0’s describing a dash pattern. For example ‘111000’.
cap
str, optional
One of the following:
‘flat_cap’
‘round_cap’
‘square_cap’
join
str, optional
One of the following:
‘bevel_join’
‘miter_join’
‘round_join’
Returns
:
bool

connect_p1
(
shape
:
object
,
position
:
str
,
connector
:
int
)
→
bool
#
Connects the first point of the line to the given shape. The specific connection can either be selected using the “position” argument or the “connector” argument.
Parameters
:
shape
object
The shape on which to connect the line. One of the shape types provided in the report module.
position
str, optional
The following values are accepted. Only a subset of the available options is supported for each shape type.
‘top’
‘right’
‘bottom’
‘left’
‘top_left’
‘top_right’
‘bottom_right’
‘bottom_left’
connector
int, optional
The accepted integer values depend on the type of shape that the line connects to.
When connected to a rectangle the accepted values are 0-3. They correspond to the middle position of each side with 0 being the top, 1 the left, 2 the bottom and 3 the right side.
When connected to a triangle the accepted values are 0-5. 0, 2 and 4 correspond to the corners whereas 1,3 and 5 to the middle positions of the triangle’s sides.
When connected to an ellipse the accepted values are 0-7, one for every 45 degrees. 0 corresponds to the top of the ellipse.
Returns
:
bool
connect_p2
(
shape
:
object
,
position
:
str
,
connector
:
int
)
→
bool
#
Connects the second point of the line to the given shape. The specific connection can either be selected using the “position” argument or the “connector” argument.
Parameters
:
shape
object
The shape on which to connect the line. One of the shape types provided in the report module.
position
str, optional
The following values are accepted. Only a subset of the available options is supported for each shape type.
‘top’
‘right’
‘bottom’
‘left’
‘top_left’
‘top_right’
‘bottom_right’
‘bottom_left’
connector
int, optional
The accepted integer values depend on the type of shape that the line connects to.
When connected to a rectangle the accepted values are 0-3. They correspond to the middle position of each side with 0 being the top, 1 the left, 2 the bottom and 3 the right side.
When connected to a triangle the accepted values are 0-5. 0, 2 and 4 correspond to the corners whereas 1,3 and 5 to the middle positions of the triangle’s sides.
When connected to an ellipse the accepted values are 0-7, one for every 45 degrees. 0 corresponds to the top of the ellipse.
Returns
:
bool
set_name
(
name
:
str
)
→
bool
#
Set the shape name.
Parameters
:
name
str
Returns
:
bool

)

class
ansa.report.
Picture
(
report_name
:
str
,

:
str
,

:
str
)
#
A picture in a report in META.
Parameters
:
report_name
str
Report Composer window name.
slide_name
str
Slide name.
shape_name
str
Shape name.
Returns
:
None
name
:
str
=
None
#
Shape name.
slide_name
:
str
=
None
#
Slide name.
report_name
:
str
=
None
#
Report Composer window name.
get_report
(
)
→
Report
#
Return the report that this shape belongs to.
Returns
:
Report
meta.report.Report
get_slide
(
)
→
Slide
#
Return the slide that this shape belongs to.
Returns
:
Slide
meta.report.Slide
get_position
(
unit
:
str
)
→
Iterable
[
float
]
#
Return the coordinates of the top left corner of the shape.
Parameters
:
unit
str, optional
Unit of the returned coordinates.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions
Returns
:
Iterable[float]
List that contains the x an y coordinates.
set_position
(
position
:
Iterable
[
float
]
,
unit
:
str
)
→
bool
#
Set the top left corner position of the shape.
Parameters
:
position
Iterable[float]
Either a list or 2-tuple that contains the desired coordinates of the top left corner of the shape.
unit
str, optional
Unit of the given coordinates.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions
Returns
:
bool

)

#
Set various line style options. All arguments are optional, any number of them can be used. The result is visible only when fill is ‘solid_line’.
Parameters
:
fill
str, optional
The available values are:
- ‘no_line’
- ‘solid_line’
color
windows.Color, optional
meta.windows.Color
width
float, optional
Line width.
dash
str, optional
One of the following predefined dash patterns:
‘solid_line’
‘dash_line’
‘dot_line’
‘dash_dot_line’
‘lg_dash_line’
‘lg_dash_dot_line’
‘lg_dash_dot_dot_line’
‘sys_dash_line’
‘sys_dash_dot_line’
‘sys_dash_dot_dot_line’
‘sys_dot_line’
‘custom_dash_line’
custom_dash_pattern
str, optional
A series of 1’s and 0’s describing a dash pattern. For example ‘111000’.
cap
str, optional
One of the following:
‘flat_cap’
‘round_cap’
‘square_cap’
join
str, optional
One of the following:
‘bevel_join’
‘miter_join’
‘round_join’

Background fill options. Fill can be either empty (‘no_fill’), have a solid color fill (‘solid_fill’), or have a background image (‘picture_fill’). The solid color option requires a valid color argument while the background image option requires a valid filename argument.

[
float
]
#
Return the coordinates of the top left corner of the shape.
Parameters
:
unit
str, optional
Unit of the returned coordinates.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions
Returns
:
Iterable[float]
List that contains the x and y coordinates.

]
,

)

Set the top left corner position of the shape.
Parameters
:
position
Iterable[float]
Either a list or 2-tuple that contains the desired coordinates of the top left corner of the shape.
unit
str, optional
Unit of the given coordinates.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions

- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions

#
Return the coordinates of the top left corner of the shape.
Parameters
:

str, optional
Unit of the returned coordinates.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions

#
Set various line style options. All arguments are optional, any number of them can be used. The result is visible only when fill is ‘solid_line’.
Parameters
:
fill
str, optional
The available values are:
- ‘no_line’
- ‘solid_line’
color
windows.Color, optional
meta.windows.Color
width
float, optional
Line width.
dash
str, optional
One of the following predefined dash patterns:
‘solid_line’
‘dash_line’
‘dot_line’
‘dash_dot_line’
‘lg_dash_line’
‘lg_dash_dot_line’
‘lg_dash_dot_dot_line’
‘sys_dash_line’
‘sys_dash_dot_line’
‘sys_dash_dot_dot_line’
‘sys_dot_line’
‘custom_dash_line’
custom_dash_pattern
str, optional
A series of 1’s and 0’s describing a dash pattern. For example ‘111000’.
cap
str, optional
One of the following:
‘flat_cap’
‘round_cap’
‘square_cap’
join
str, optional
One of the following:
‘bevel_join’
‘miter_join’
‘round_join’
Returns
:
bool

(

:
str
,
color
:
windows.Color
,
filename
:
str
)
→
bool
#
Background fill options. Fill can be either empty (‘no_fill’), have a solid color fill (‘solid_fill’), or have a background image (‘picture_fill’). The solid color option requires a valid color argument while the background image option requires a valid filename argument.
Parameters
:
fill
str
Supported values are:
‘no_fill’
‘solid_fill’
‘picture_fill’
color
windows.Color, optional
meta.windows.Color
filename
str, optional
Filename pointing to an image file.
Returns
:
bool

Return the coordinates of the top left corner of the shape.

Unit of the returned coordinates.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.

- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions

Set various line style options. All arguments are optional, any number of them can be used. The result is visible only when fill is ‘solid_line’.

- ‘no_line’
- ‘solid_line’

meta.windows.Color

‘solid_line’
‘dash_line’

‘dash_dot_line’
‘lg_dash_line’
‘lg_dash_dot_line’
‘lg_dash_dot_dot_line’
‘sys_dash_line’

‘sys_dash_dot_dot_line’
‘sys_dot_line’
‘custom_dash_line’

‘round_cap’

Background fill options. Fill can be either empty (‘no_fill’), have a solid color fill (‘solid_fill’), or have a background image (‘picture_fill’). The solid color option requires a valid color argument while the background image option requires a valid filename argument.

‘no_fill’

get_text_style
(
position
:
int
)
→
dict
#
Returns the text style in the form of a python dictionary. The dictionary contains the same keys and can be applied directly to the set_text_style function. An optional position argument can be used to return the style of a specific character in the text.
Parameters
:
position
int, optional
Index of the character in the text whose style is returned. Indexing starts at 1. If undefined the style of the last character is returned.
Returns
:
dict
Python dictionary with the following text style options.
font_family     string
font_size       integer
bold            boolean
italic          boolean
underline       boolean
strike_through  boolean
superscript     boolean
subscript       boolean
text_color      meta.windows.Color
text_align      string    (‘left’, ‘center’, ‘right’, ‘justify’)
shape_align     string    (‘top’, ‘middle’, ‘bottom’, ‘top_center’, ‘middle_center’, ‘bottom_center’)
autofit         string    (‘no_autofit’, ‘shrink_text_on_overflow’, ‘resize_shape_to_fit_text’)
wrap            boolean

)

:

)
→

[
float
]
#
Return the coordinates of the top left corner of the ellipse.
Parameters
:
unit
str, optional
Unit of the returned coordinates.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions
Returns
:
Iterable[float]
List that contains the x and y coordinates.

float
]

)

unit
str, optional
Unit of the given coordinates.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions

#
Set various line style options. All arguments are optional, any number of them can be used. The result is visible only when fill is ‘solid_line’.
Parameters
:
fill
str, optional
The available values are:
- ‘no_line’
- ‘solid_line’
color
windows.Color, optional
meta.windows.Color
width
float, optional
Line width.
dash
str, optional
One of the following predefined dash patterns:
‘solid_line’
‘dash_line’
‘dot_line’
‘dash_dot_line’
‘lg_dash_line’
‘lg_dash_dot_line’
‘lg_dash_dot_dot_line’
‘sys_dash_line’
‘sys_dash_dot_line’
‘sys_dash_dot_dot_line’
‘sys_dot_line’
‘custom_dash_line’
custom_dash_pattern
str, optional
A series of 1’s and 0’s describing a dash pattern. For example ‘111000’.
cap
str, optional
One of the following:
‘flat_cap’
‘round_cap’
‘square_cap’
join
str, optional
One of the following:
‘bevel_join’
‘miter_join’
‘round_join’
Returns
:
bool

#
Background fill options. Fill can be either empty (‘no_fill’), have a solid color fill (‘solid_fill’), or have a background image (‘picture_fill’). The solid color option requires a valid color argument while the background image option requires a valid filename argument.
Parameters
:
fill
str
Supported values are:
‘no_fill’
‘solid_fill’
‘picture_fill’

windows.Color, optional
meta.windows.Color

get_text_style
(
position
:
int
)
→
dict
#
Returns the text style in the form of a python dictionary. The dictionary contains the same keys and can be applied directly to the set_text_style function. An optional position argument can be used to return the style of a specific character in the text.
Parameters
:
position
int, optional
Index of the character in the text whose style is returned. Indexing starts at 1. If undefined the style of the last character is returned.
Returns
:
dict
Python dictionary with the following text style options.font_family     stringfont_size       integerbold            booleanitalic          booleanunderline       booleanstrike_through  booleansuperscript     booleansubscript       booleantext_color      meta.windows.Colortext_align      string                        ‘left’                        ‘center’                        ‘right’                        ‘justify’shape_align     string                        ‘top’                        ‘middle’                        ‘bottom’                        ‘top_center’                        ‘middle_center’                        ‘bottom_center’autofit         string                        ‘no_autofit’                        ‘shrink_text_on_overflow’                        ‘resize_shape_to_fit_text’wrap            boolean

)

bool

- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions

#
Set various line style options. All arguments are optional, any number of them can be used. The result is visible only when fill is ‘solid_line’.
Parameters
:
fill
str, optional
The available values are:
- ‘no_line’
- ‘solid_line’
color
windows.Color, optional
meta.windows.Color
width
float, optional
Line width.
dash
str, optional
One of the following predefined dash patterns:
‘solid_line’
‘dash_line’
‘dot_line’
‘dash_dot_line’
‘lg_dash_line’
‘lg_dash_dot_line’
‘lg_dash_dot_dot_line’
‘sys_dash_line’
‘sys_dash_dot_line’
‘sys_dash_dot_dot_line’
‘sys_dot_line’
‘custom_dash_line’
custom_dash_pattern
str, optional
A series of 1’s and 0’s describing a dash pattern. For example ‘111000’.
cap
str, optional
One of the following:
‘flat_cap’
‘round_cap’
‘square_cap’
join
str, optional
One of the following:
‘bevel_join’
‘miter_join’
‘round_join’

get_text_style
(
position
:
int
)
→
dict
#
Returns the text style in the form of a python dictionary. The dictionary contains the same keys and can be applied directly to the set_text_style function. An optional position argument can be used to return the style of a specific character in the text.
Parameters
:
position
int, optional
Index of the character in the text whose style is returned. Indexing starts at 1. If undefined the style of the last character is returned.
Returns
:
dict
Python dictionary with the following text style options.font_family     stringfont_size       integerbold            booleanitalic          booleanunderline       booleanstrike_through  booleansuperscript     booleansubscript       booleantext_color      meta.windows.Colortext_align      string                        ‘left’                        ‘center’                        ‘right’                        ‘justify’shape_align     string                        ‘top’                        ‘middle’                        ‘bottom’                        ‘top_center’                        ‘middle_center’                        ‘bottom_center’autofit         string                        ‘no_autofit’                        ‘shrink_text_on_overflow’                        ‘resize_shape_to_fit_text’wrap            boolean

class
ansa.report.
TableRange
(
report_name
:
str
,
slide_name
:
str
,
shape_name
:
str
,
top_left
:
list
,
bottom_right
:
list
)
#
A range of cells on a table in a report in META. The range is a contiguous rectangle of cells. It is represented by the minimum row and column of the cells (top left corner), and the maximum row and column (bottom right corner).
Parameters
:
report_name
str
Report Composer window name.
slide_name
str
Slide name.
shape_name
str
Shape name.
top_left
list
Minimum row and column of the cells (top left corner).
bottom_right
list
Maximum row and column (bottom right corner).
Returns
:
None
name
:
str
=
None
#
Shape name.
slide_name
:
str
=
None
#
Slide name.
report_name
:
str
=
None
#
Report Composer window name.
min_row
:
int
=
None
#
min_column
:
int
=
None
#
max_row
:
int
=
None
#
max_column
:
int
=
None
#
set_text
(
text
:
str
)
→
bool
#
Set the text for every cell in the range. Accepts html for formatting.
Parameters
:
text
str
Returns
:
bool

#
Set text style options. All arguments are optional. Any number of them can be used.
Parameters
:
font_family
str, optional
See corresponding setting in GUI for the available fonts.

int, optional
See corresponding setting in GUI for size values.
bold
bool, optional

bool, optional

meta.windows.Color

The following values are supported:
‘left’

‘justify’
shape_align

The following values are supported:
‘top’
‘middle’

‘top_center’
‘middle_center’
‘bottom_center’

:
bool

Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.

- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’

Background fill options. Fill can be either empty (‘no_fill’), have a solid color fill (‘solid_fill’), or have a background image (‘picture_fill’). The solid color option requires a valid color argument while the background image option requires a valid filename argument.

#
Background fill options. Fill can be either empty (‘no_fill’), have a solid color fill (‘solid_fill’), or have a background image (‘picture_fill’). The solid color option requires a valid color argument while the background image option requires a valid filename argument.
Parameters
:
fill
str
Supported values are:
‘no_fill’
‘solid_fill’
‘picture_fill’
color
windows.Color, optional
meta.windows.Color
filename
str, optional
Path to an image file.
Returns
:
bool
get_text_style
(
position
:
int
)
→
dict
#
Returns the text style in the form of a python dictionary. The dictionary contains the same keys and can be applied directly to the set_text_style function. An optional position argument can be used to return the style of a specific character in the text.
Parameters
:
position
int, optional
Index of the character in the text whose style is returned. Indexing starts at 1. If undefined the style of the last character is returned.
Returns
:
dict
Python dictionary with the following text style options.              font_family     string              font_size       integer              bold            boolean              italic          boolean              underline       boolean              strike_through  boolean              superscript     boolean              subscript       boolean              text_color      meta.windows.Color              text_align      string                                    ‘left’                                    ‘center’                                    ‘right’                                    ‘justify’              shape_align     string                                    ‘top’                                    ‘middle’                                    ‘bottom’                                    ‘top_center’                                    ‘middle_center’                                    ‘bottom_center’              autofit         string                                    ‘no_autofit’                                    ‘shrink_text_on_overflow’                                    ‘resize_shape_to_fit_text’              wrap            boolean

class
ansa.report.
ReportFilter
(
type
:
str
,
name
:
str
,
operator
:
str
,
value
:
str
,
value2
:
str
)
#
A ReportFilter object is used to find pptx files based on their tags. There are four possible types of ReportFilter objects (as specified by the first argument in the constructor): ‘presentation’, ‘slide’, ‘element’, and ‘tag’.
ReportFilter objects of type ‘tag’ that specify a tag name, an operator such as ‘equal’, and a value represent specific rules by which to match tags. The other three types of ReportFilter objects, namely ‘presentation’, ‘slide’, and ‘element’ specify whether the search should match presentation tags, slide tags or element tags accordingly. This is achieved by adding the desired ‘tag’ object as a child of the corresponding ‘presentation’, ‘slide’, or ‘element’ object.
The tree structure can be expanded to achieve more complex matching rules.
Constructor Arguments
type      string                Available values are listed below. Note that the ‘tag’ type also requires the rest of the arguments to be specified, a name, operator, and at least one value (depending on the operator).
‘presentation’
‘slide’
‘element’
‘tag’
name      string    (optional)  The tag name to search for.
operator  string    (optional)  Available values are listed below, note that some operators require a value2 argument as well.
‘equal’
‘less’
‘greater’
‘less_equal’
‘greater_equal’
‘not_equal’
‘between’
‘not_between’
‘contains’
‘not_contains’
‘starts_with’
‘not_starts_with’
‘ends_with’
‘not_ends_with’
‘reg_expression’
‘not_reg_expression’
value     string    (optional)  The tag value that is matched against the value of the tags in the report files using the specified operator.
value2    string    (optional)  A second optional value required by operators  ‘between’ and ‘not_between’.
Parameters
:
type
str
Available values are listed below. Note that the ‘tag’ type also requires the rest of the arguments to be specified, a name, operator, and at least one value (depending on the operator).
‘presentation’
‘slide’
‘element’
‘tag’
name
str, optional
The tag name to search for.
operator
str, optional
Available values are listed below, note that some operators require a value2 argument as well.
‘equal’
‘less’
‘greater’
‘less_equal’
‘greater_equal’
‘not_equal’
‘between’
‘not_between’
‘contains’
‘not_contains’
‘starts_with’
‘not_starts_with’
‘ends_with’
‘not_ends_with’
‘reg_expression’
‘not_reg_expression’
value
str, optional
The tag value that is matched against the value of the tags in the report files using the specified operator.
value2
str, optional
A second optional value required by operators  ‘between’ and ‘not_between’.
Returns
:
None
search
(
directory
:
str
,
folder_filter
:
str
,
file_filter
:
str
,
search_in_subfolders
:
bool
)
→
Iterable
[
str
]
#
Finds pptx files whose tags match this filter, in the specified folder. Files can also be optionally filtered by their name using the file_filter option. Subfolders can be optionally search and filtered as well using the corresponding options.
Parameters
:
directory
str
Search directory.
folder_filter
str, optional
A string to filter the sub-folders by their name. An ‘*’ corresponds to any sub-string in the folder name. This argument is used only when search_in_subfolders is True. As an example a value of ‘arp*’ will match folders whose name begins with ‘arp’.
file_filter
str, optional
A string to filter the pptx files based on their name. An ‘*’ corresponds to any sub-string in the file name. As an example a value of ‘arp*’ will match files whose name begins with ‘arp’.
search_in_subfolders
bool, optional
Whether to search sub-folders. Default value is False.
Returns
:
Iterable[str]
List of matching pptx file-paths
get_children
(
)
→
Iterable
[
ReportFilter
]
#
Returns a list with the children of this filter.
Returns
:
Iterable[ReportFilter]
List of report.ReportFilter objects

:

Set various line style options. All arguments are optional, any number of them can be used. The result is visible only when fill is ‘solid_line’.

- ‘solid_line’

bool
#
Background fill options. Fill can be either empty (‘no_fill’), have a solid color fill (‘solid_fill’), or have a background image (‘picture_fill’). The solid color option requires a valid color argument while the background image option requires a valid filename argument.
Parameters
:
fill
str
Supported values are:
‘no_fill’
‘solid_fill’
‘picture_fill’
color
windows.Color, optional
meta.windows.Color
filename
str, optional
Path to an image file.
Returns
:
bool

get_points
(

:
str
)
→
list
#
Returns a list of the points of this shape. The points are optionally converted to the desired unit.
Parameters
:
unit
str, optional
Unit of the returned width and height.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions
Returns
:
list
A list of x, y pairs in the requested units.
set_points
(
points
:
list
,
unit
:
str
)
→
bool
#

Parameters
:
points
list
A non-empty list of pairs of x, y coordinates.
unit
str, optional
Unit of the given width and height.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions
Returns
:
bool
get_text_style
(
position
:
int
)
→
dict
#
Returns the text style in the form of a python dictionary. The dictionary contains the same keys and can be applied directly to the set_text_style function. An optional position argument can be used to return the style of a specific character in the text.
Parameters
:
position
int, optional
Index of the character in the text whose style is returned. Indexing starts at 1. If undefined the style of the last character is returned.
Returns
:
dict
Python dictionary with the following text style options.font_family     stringfont_size       integerbold            booleanitalic          booleanunderline       booleanstrike_through  booleansuperscript     booleansubscript       booleantext_color      meta.windows.Colortext_align      string                        ‘left’                        ‘center’                        ‘right’                        ‘justify’shape_align     string                        ‘top’                        ‘middle’                        ‘bottom’                        ‘top_center’                        ‘middle_center’                        ‘bottom_center’autofit         string                        ‘no_autofit’                        ‘shrink_text_on_overflow’                        ‘resize_shape_to_fit_text’wrap            boolean

)

class
ansa.report.
Model3D
(
report_name
:
str
,
slide_name
:
str
,
shape_name
:
str
)
#
A 3d model in a report in META.
Parameters
:
report_name
str
Report Composer window name.
slide_name
str
Slide name.
shape_name
str
Shape name.
Returns
:
None
name
:
str
=
None
#

class
ansa.report.
Audio
(
report_name
:
str
,
slide_name
:
str
,
shape_name
:
str
)
#
An audio shape in a report in META.
Parameters
:
report_name
str
Report Composer window name.
slide_name
str
Slide name.
shape_name
str
Shape name.
Returns
:
None
name
:
str
=
None
#
Shape name.
slide_name
:
str
=
None
#
Slide name.
report_name
:
str
=
None
#
Report Composer window name.
get_report
(
)
→
Report
#
Return the report that this shape belongs to.
Returns
:
Report
meta.report.Report
get_slide
(
)
→
Slide
#
Return the slide that this shape belongs to.
Returns
:
Slide
meta.report.Slide
get_position
(
unit
:
str
)
→
Iterable
[
float
]
#
Return the coordinates of the top left corner of the shape.
Parameters
:
unit
str, optional
Unit of the returned coordinates.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions
Returns
:
Iterable[float]
List that contains the x and y coordinates.
set_position
(
position
:
Iterable
[
float
]
,
unit
:
str
)
→
bool
#
Set the top left corner position of the shape.
Parameters
:
position
Iterable[float]
Either a list or 2-tuple that contains the desired coordinates of the top left corner of the shape.
unit
str, optional
Unit of the given coordinates.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions
Returns
:
bool
get_size
(
unit
:
str
)
→
Iterable
[
float
]
#
Returns the width and height of the shape.
Parameters
:
unit
str, optional
Unit of the returned width and height.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions
Returns
:
Iterable[float]
A list that contains the width and height in the requested units.
set_size
(
size
:
Iterable
[
float
]
,
unit
:
str
)
→
bool
#
Set the shape width and height.
Parameters
:
size
Iterable[float]
Either a list or 2-tuple that contains the width and height.
unit
str, optional
Unit of the given width and height.
Available values are listed below. The default value is ‘norm’.
- ‘emu’
- ‘cm’
- ‘mm’
- ‘inch’
- ‘pt’
- ‘pc’
- ‘pixel’
- ‘norm’ : Values normalized to slide dimensions
Returns
:
bool

)
→
bool

Place shape in front of the other shapes in the slide.

:
bool

)

bool
#
Returns the visibility status of the shape.

:

Sets the visibility status of the shape.
Parameters

True makes the shape visible. False makes the shape hidden.
